2. **Where does she now place Xavier on the trustworthy-betrayer axis?** The *Deadly Genesis* concealment was an integrative wound; her splitting defense routed him to "betrayer" with insufficient middle ground. Post-resurrection, with distance and Xavier's own continued moral degradation across separate arcs, the question is whether she has constructed an *integrated* image of him (the growth move) or simply consolidated the devaluation (the static move). A surveillance read would look for whether she keeps any physical token of him in her quarters; presence or absence is high-signal.
3. **Does she still want children / dynastic continuation?** Never directly addressed in canon. Given the family-line-as-curse framing she carries, the answer is non-obvious and important: a Lilandra who decides the Neramani line should *end with her* is a fundamentally different political actor than one who is searching for an heir.
4. **What is her actual relationship to her own faith?** The military-religious order she joined as a young woman is treated in canon as career architecture; whether she retains private devotional practice is unclear. If she does, it is a regulatory resource the file is currently underweighting.
5. **How does she now metabolize the Vulcan episode specifically?** Vulcan was her nephew-by-marriage, her brother's murderer, her own captor, and a victim of Xavier's concealment — a single figure carrying four incompatible relational valences. Her processing of this knot is the unresolved psychological project of the late record.

---

### 7.5 Fork Points — The Specific Triggers That Will Decide Which Branch Activates

Forecasting in this subject is event-driven more than time-driven. The following are the discrete triggers whose resolution will collapse the probability distribution above onto a single fork.

- **Trigger 1: The next succession crisis in the Empire.** Whoever currently holds or contests the throne will produce a vacancy or a stabilization within a forecastable window. If vacancy → Fork A or C activates. If stabilization under a reformist not-her → Fork B becomes available. If stabilization under a regressive → Fork B or D.
- **Trigger 2: Xavier's next major moral event.** A redemption arc moves her toward integration (growth). A further fall confirms the devaluation and pushes Fork C or D.
- **Trigger 3: Deathbird's next move.** Reconciliation, attack, or death of the sister each produce categorically different downstream psychologies. Deathbird's death without reconciliation is the single most depressively-loaded possible event in her life and pushes hard toward D.
- **Trigger 4: A second assassination attempt, successful or not.** Survival of a second attempt either consolidates her (rare, growth-aligned: "I have already died once") or shatters her (more common: re-traumatization compounds geometrically). Whether she had completed convalescence from the first death at the moment of the second attempt is the determining variable.
- **Trigger 5: Direct encounter with a *young* reformist she could mentor.** Underrated trigger. The presence of a viable successor figure is the single most reliable route to Fork B; absent that figure she cannot psychologically permit herself to step aside.

---

### 7.6 What Pushes Her Toward Growth

Growth, for this subject, is not happiness — it is the *breaking of the loop*. Specifically: dissolving the duty-equals-worth fusion, integrating the split images of Xavier and of her family, and learning to distinguish rescuer from partner.

The interventions and conditions that move her in that direction:

- **A relationship structured as genuine peer-equality from the outset, not as rescue.** Her pattern of fusing with rescuers is the deepest single distortion in her relational repertoire. A relationship — romantic, collegial, or mentoring-reciprocal — initiated under conditions where neither party saved the other rewrites the template. She is in her sixties of subjective experience and has never had one. The Starjammer captain, oddly, is the canonical figure closest to this possibility because the rescue-vector ran the other direction.
- **A reform project she can hand to a successor.** As noted in Fork A's growth-marker: the moment she designs institutions that outlast her is the moment she ceases to need the throne to be a self.
- **Confrontation with the reformist-on-conquest-throne contradiction in a setting she cannot exit by retreating into protocol.** Sustained dialogue with, e.g., a Krakoan-mutant political theorist, a Kree dissident, or an internal Shi'ar abolitionist would force the contradiction into integrated thought rather than perpetual avoidance.
- **Therapeutic-grade processing of the maternal murder.** The earliest unmetabolized wound. Her culture lacks an institution for this; an outsider (Krakoan healer, Earth-trained psychotherapist, or telepathic-empathic ally) is the only plausible vector.
- **Time spent in a role with no ceremony at all.** A horticultural project, an apprenticeship, a stretch of manual or domestic labor — any sustained interval in which she is not *Majestrix-something* — directly attacks the role-encapsulation defense and would yield disproportionate gains.

---

### 7.7 What Pushes Her Toward Catastrophe

Catastrophe is Fork C (managerial authoritarianism) or Fork D (terminal withdrawal). The conditions that accelerate either:

- **Repeated betrayal by trusted intimates within a compressed window.** Her trust-default is a finite resource; betrayals do not average, they *accumulate*. Two betrayals within a convalescent window do more damage than four betrayals across decades.
- **Loss of role concurrent with loss of bondmate.** The two load-bearing structures must not fail simultaneously. If they do, the depressive collapse is severe and the reconstitution may not occur.
- **A security crisis that *seems* to justify expanded executive power.** This is the canonical authoritarian trap and her intellectualization defense is precisely calibrated to rationalize her way into it. A genuine Brood-class or Phoenix-class external threat during a period of imperial restoration is the most dangerous possible context — she will accept emergency powers "until the crisis passes," and the crisis will not pass cleanly.
- **Vindication of D'Ken or Deathbird in any framing.** If history, court, or circumstance ever produces a narrative in which her siblings' brutality is retrospectively justified, the foundational reaction-formation that organizes her ethics destabilizes. She does not know who she is if they were right.
- **Isolation from non-Shi'ar input.** Her cross-cultural humility is a regulatory resource. An Empire-internal restoration that severs her from Earth, the Starjammers, and the broader cosmic polity removes the corrective mirror and accelerates Fork C.
- **A second assassination during convalescence.** Discussed above. The compounding is non-linear.

---

### 7.8 The Structural Tragedy and Its Only Real Exit

The honest forecast must acknowledge what §1–6 of this dossier have already established: her virtues are *structurally incompatible* with the institution she keeps trying to reform from the top. A conquest empire selects against its own reformist sovereigns; this is not bad luck across her iterations, it is the loop's selection pressure. Every restoration is therefore a deferred deposition, and the cycle terminates only in one of three ways:

1. **The Empire transforms** (low probability within her lifetime even extended; would require concurrent reformist pressure she does not control).
2. **She exits the Empire** (Fork B; psychologically optimal, politically resisted by her own reform-impulse).
3. **She is consumed by the Empire** (Forks C or D; the loop's default terminus).

The growth path is therefore not "rule better." It is "stop ruling, and build something the next reformer can inherit." Whether she is capable of that recognition is the central forward-question this file cannot yet answer — but the resurrection event has, for the first time, given her the existential distance from her own office that might make the recognition possible. A Lilandra who has *already died for the throne once* has, in principle, the standing to refuse to die for it again.

Whether she uses that standing is the watch-item.

---

### 7.9 Surveillance Priorities Going Forward

For continued file maintenance, prioritize the following observables in descending order of forecast-value:

1. Sleeping-quarters stability and door-orientation patterns (hypervigilance baseline).
2. Public-address frequency and platform architecture (assassination-recovery curve).
3. Presence/absence of Xavier-associated personal objects in private space (integration vs. devaluation marker).
4. Frequency of unmediated contact with non-Shi'ar advisors (corrective-mirror retention).
5. Designation or non-designation of formal successors (loop-break readiness).
6. Tone shift in references to D'Ken and Deathbird — specifically whether she begins to *explain* them rather than *contrast* herself against them (reaction-formation status).
7. Whether she resumes any private devotional practice (latent regulatory resource activation).
8. Length and content of any sustained period spent doing work that has no ceremonial dimension (role-encapsulation flex).

The file remains open. The next entry should be triggered by the first of the §7.5 events to occur.

## Relationship Graph
### [[Charles Francis Xavier (Professor X)]]
- Bonded partner across light-years from first telepathic contact (UXM #97) — experienced as soul-recognition, not romance-as-growth
- Constructed secure base; the entire architecture of her adult affect regulation rests on this single bond
- Moral counselor whose counsel she weighs disproportionately and against whom she sometimes rules in full protocol (Phoenix verdict)
- FAILURE MODE: any actor with leverage on Xavier has leverage on her judgment; prolonged separation accelerates her decompensation curve on a measurable timeline; if the bond were ever to curdle — if Xavier were revealed as having truly betrayed the trust (Deadly Genesis / Vulcan revelations approach this) — she would not split into devaluation, she would intensify into prophetic certainty about him as a problem to be solved; the closer the bond, the more catastrophic its weaponization
- LEVERAGE: route any persuasion through him; threaten him to destabilize her; remove him to break her

### Deathbird
- Sister, eldest, fratricide (killed Adari), recurring usurper
- Lilandra cannot execute her — has captured her multiple times and spared her every time
- FAILURE MODE: the standing exception that proves every rule of her sovereignty; Deathbird knows this and uses it; the relationship will never resolve because Lilandra refuses to do to a sister what a sister would do to her
- LEVERAGE: any operation involving Deathbird as captive triggers the spare-reflex; any operation involving Deathbird as threat triggers Lilandra's most reliable distraction

### Dken
- Elder brother, parricide, original tyrant whose M'Kraan plot she defected to stop
- Broken by M'Kraan exposure, removed from the board but not resolved as family
- FAILURE MODE: he is the proof-of-concept for her entire life-project (the worst Neramani must not hold the throne); his existence justifies her coronation and also indicts it
- LEVERAGE: invocation of D'Ken's name reactivates the defector-identity that organizes her

### Vulcan
- Third Summers brother, secret Xavier project, usurper, husband-killer
- The Neramani-by-marriage equivalent she failed to anticipate — the betrayal she did not see coming because it came through Xavier's blind spot, not her family's
- FAILURE MODE: she dies in the assassination attempt against him; her end-state behavior is her origin-state behavior, fugitive Majestrix
- LEVERAGE: Vulcan represents the limit case of her institutional-trust failure mode

### Jean Grey Phoenix
- Pronounced death on her in full protocol; offered Arin'nn Haelar
- FAILURE MODE: Phoenix-coded stimuli override her proportional judgment for the rest of her life — Phoenix-mania arc proceeds directly from this verdict's unresolved residue
- LEVERAGE: anything Phoenix-coded — invocation, manifestation, prophecy — moves her without further argument

### Gladiator Kallark
- Praetor of the Imperial Guard, sworn to office not person
- Procedurally loyal; will execute her overthrow if office passes; will defend her if office holds
- FAILURE MODE: her failure to cultivate his personal loyalty (because she does not cultivate personal loyalists) means his sword turns with the throne, not with her
- LEVERAGE: control the legitimacy of office and you control Gladiator; control Gladiator and Lilandra loses her sword

### Imperial Council
- Convened deliberative body she genuinely trusts to share her premise of legitimate rule
- FAILURE MODE: most do not share the premise; she keeps expecting them to
- LEVERAGE: faction the council and she will underread it

### The Xmen
- Inter-species respect, procedurally extended, repeatedly re-extended after every catastrophe
- FAILURE MODE: she will choose Empire over Earth at the decisive moment, then quietly arrange for Earth to survive the choice
- LEVERAGE: appeal to her as the only Shi'ar who treats Terrans as moral equals
